You are still instructed to report the date of commencement of use for verification, and to destroy the old seals by cutting off the corners. This order, etc., is hereby issued, and each copper seal is attached for your compliance with the instructions, fixing the sixth as the date of uniform commencement of use, and reporting the date of commencement of use and destroying the old seals by cutting off the corners. This order.

Three Countries Send More Warships to China

Recently, the British added two first-class destroyers, No. 7 and No. 59, from Hong Kong to Shanghai. They immediately sailed to Nanjing to prepare to go to Jiujiang, Hankou, and other places if necessary. The United States also increased the number of destroyers sent to Shanghai from Little Luzon by four. The USS Shefferson and USS Panay arrived yesterday, and another ship will be sent to the Yangtze River today. In addition, Japan dispatched the 24th Destroyer Squadron, the Yanagi, Hinoki, Momo, and Kashi ships, from Sasebo, which telegraphed Shanghai yesterday that they had left Japan and would arrive in Shanghai today. One ship, the Atami, has been dispatched to the Daye area, and 300 marines will arrive in Shanghai today. A small team will be sent upstream to protect navigation and foreigners.

Decline in Yangtze River Shipping

Hunan Goods Returned to Hankou

Since July 25th, Hunan has not traded goods. Most of the goods shipped from Shanghai to Hunan have been turned back midway. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson received a telegram from Hankou stating that a large batch of goods bound for Changsha was loaded by the Hankou-He wheel on July 25th and brought several large iron barges full of various goods into Hunan to above Yuezhou, then immediately turned back to Hankou and remained on the ship, waiting for the situation in Hunan to stabilize before being transported again.

Yangtze River Goods Are Hit Hard

The import and export business of the Yangtze River ships of the Shanghai Six Companies has been hit hard recently. All goods above Wuhu have virtually stopped. In the past week, except for sugar and salt, which are occasionally loaded, most of the other miscellaneous goods are being loaded in. In recent days, the British and Japanese giant ships on the Yangtze River line, which could transport more than 10,000 pieces of export goods in half a day, are now only loading more than 1,000 pieces. The decline in business is unprecedented.

New British Ship Delays Opening

The Baohe, a Yangtze River oil engine express ship being built by Jardine Matheson at the Jiangnan Shipyard in Shanghai, is the same size as the Taikoo's new ship Wuhu and is also on the Shanghai-Yichang route. It was originally planned to leave the factory and be launched on the 15th of last month, but due to the current situation, the project has not been completed, so the opening date has been delayed. The comprador has assigned Shi Yuzhang to fill the position, and it is estimated that the ship will be launched and start sailing soon.

The Truth About the Da Zhong Ship Accident

Location: Fuzhou in Kwantung Bay

Entrusted to the South Manchuria Railway Shipyard for Salvage

The Da Zhong ship of Heng'an Company in this port had an accident on the way, as reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the location of the ship accident is in Fuzhou, not Fuzhou in Fujian Province. The following is a breakdown of the latest information obtained yesterday:

Location of the Reef

It has been found that the Da Zhong ship left Zhenjiang for Liaoning Fuzhou on July 26 to load coal to be transported to Shanghai and then unloaded at Jiangyin. The ship encountered a hurricane on the sea after leaving. By July 30, when the ship arrived in Fuzhou in the east, between Murchison Island and Milne Island at 121 degrees 12 minutes east longitude and 39 degrees 06 minutes north latitude, it was hit by a large storm. Around 1:00 AM on the 31st, the ship was hit by wind and waves and ran aground on a hidden reef on the island. The head cabin of the ship was driven by the waves to run aground on the reef stones for 40 feet. Fuzhou is a coast on the Liaodong Peninsula and an important coastal port in the Northeast.

Loss Situation

The ship owner, Russian Zhou Cang, reported in a telegram that the Da Zhong ship accident was caused by the impact of strong winds, which made it impossible to steer. The front of the ship was blown by the wind onto the hidden reef. The head cabin was in the reef stones. The middle cabin and stern were not yet in the reef, so the front of the ship was about 40 feet under water during high tide, and the stern could still float 19 feet above the water. However, the front water cabin and the bottom of the steering platform were broken and leaking water into the ship. Most importantly, the bottom of the ship was not leaking, so it was still possible to find a way to rescue it.

Towing and Rescue Measures

After Heng'an Company received the ship owner's report, it telegraphed the Dalian branch to discuss salvage plans with the South Manchuria Railway Company Shipyard. According to a telegram yesterday, the South Manchuria Railway Company Shipyard sent experienced ship masters to the accident site to survey and said that salvage was possible. The company telegraphed back to order them to salvage as soon as possible. All personnel from the ship owner and below remained on the ship to assist in the rescue. The South Manchuria Railway Company has sent engineers and water ghosts to Murchison Island to begin work. The daily towing and rescue fee is set at 750 yuan. According to the Shanghai Xing reporter, the Da Zhong ship has a net tonnage of 2,300 tons. This time, it was an empty ship accident and had not yet loaded coal, so it is hoped that it can be rescued.

Japanese Committee Member Replaced in the Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident

Shimada Takes Over

The Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident Investigation Committee has been investigating the losses of the Nanjing Incident. Because the Japanese side's demands were not supported by any evidence, it has not been resolved so far. The Japanese committee members handling this case were Consul Shimizu and lawyer Murakami. Now, Consul Shimizu has been ordered to be dismissed and has returned to his country. The Japanese committee vacancy has been officially announced by Consul General Shigemitsu yesterday, appointing Shimada, the deputy consul of the Japanese Consulate in Nanjing, to take over. In addition to notifying the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for reference, Committee Member Shimada has already come to Shanghai to receive the case files in preparation for continuing negotiations and resolving the matter as soon as possible.

Denial by the Anti-Smoking Association Regarding Opium Export from China

Yesterday's Inquiry to Various Departments for Investigation and Reply

The Central Anti-Smoking Committee, based on a report in the July 16th edition of the "North-China Daily News," stated that a large amount of opium had recently been transported to India. The Indian government had specially dispatched three commissioners to China and Japan to investigate. It was claimed that the opium was manufactured in Japan, with China serving as the central point for transshipment. The committee, considering that if the report was accurate, the harm to China would be immense, regardless of whether it was true or not, believed it had a duty to thoroughly investigate and clarify the situation. It was learned that the committee yesterday specially consulted the Ministry of Finance, ordering all customs houses to strictly investigate and seize, and consulted the provincial governments of Guangdong, Shandong, Fujian, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu to conduct thorough investigations. It also consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send letters to the authorities of various concessions along the coast for a reply.

Zhao Jinqing delivered the donation by letter to the Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee at the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road. However, due to the unstable situation, this was delayed. Joint Meeting of Wusong and Baoshan Authorities Yesterday

Record of the Mass Meeting of the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union

Resolved to Elect Eight Representatives

To Negotiate with Factory Management This Morning

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union held a general strike rally at the Public Sports Field. Over one thousand workers attended, with representatives from various unions. The city party headquarters specially sent Zhang Yunqing to provide guidance. The Public Security Bureau sent Inspector Gao from the Second District with police officers to maintain order. The key resolutions passed at the meeting and the declaration against the French Concession Police's unwarranted arrest of striking committee members are detailed below.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Xu Amei reported with great sorrow on the events of the strike in recent days. He then reported that the arrest of strike committee member Wang A'gen was a plot by the French imperialist capitalists to completely trap and harm the leaders of our striking workers so that our strike force would disappear. Since they have already arrested Wang A'gen, they certainly want to arrest all of our striking committee members. We must know that the more severely our strike struggle spirit is suppressed, the more fiercely we will struggle. It is hoped that all striking workers will work harder and fight desperately to achieve our ultimate goal. Subsequently, Zhang Amao, Chen Puai, and others gave speeches that were extremely tragic and indignant, and the atmosphere of the strike was extremely tense.

Key Resolutions

The chairman proposed a motion for the masses to discuss, and it was immediately resolved to send eight representatives, including Chen Puai, to the company this morning to directly inquire about the conditions and negotiate a solution to the strike to avoid the risk of labor and management not speaking face to face.

Declaration Issued

The assembly immediately passed a declaration against the French Concession Police's unwarranted arrest of strike committee member Wang A'gen and others (omitted above). Yesterday (the 4th), strike committee member Wang A'gen and worker Su Jianliang were walking along Route Lafayette, standing by the roadside resting, when a large number of detectives suddenly surrounded them with great force, searching their persons but finding nothing. They then accused them of being rioters, and then accused them of conspiring with others in whispers and arrested them. Who are the other people, and what are they conspiring about? How can the words "whispering" be used to falsely accuse and point them out as rioters? The capitalists' conspiracies and vicious plans to arrest our workers without cause are not only completely exposed but also use the three words "perhaps it is" to frame the workers. How can all our striking workers, while still breathing, allow others to be falsely accused? We can only vow to oppose it and ask all sectors of society to uphold justice. We are now shouting slogans: (1) Oppose the French Concession Police's unwarranted arrest of workers! Oppose the capitalists' conspiracy to frame them! (1) Oppose the French imperialist capitalists bribing the police to wantonly persecute them! (1) Oppose the French Concession Police falsely accusing Wang A'gen and Su Jianliang of being rioters! (1) Oppose the French Concession Police creating unwarranted miscarriages of justice! (1) All striking workers unite to oppose it! (1) We will never give up until the arrested workers are released!

County Construction Bureau Schedules Meeting to Discuss Telephone

Yesterday, Director Wu of the Shanghai County Construction Bureau sent an official letter to the district chiefs of the first, second, third, and sixth districts of Puxi in the county, stating: "Regarding the establishment of long-distance telephone lines within the county, the county government meeting previously approved and instructed this bureau to plan and implement the project. Currently, the section in Beiqiao has been fully equipped, and the section in Tangbei is also under planning. However, partial implementation takes a long time and costs more. Both economy and time are wasted. It is neither a quick solution nor a way to comprehensively plan the overall situation. Moreover, only communication between sections is possible, and it is not possible to communicate with the city of Shanghai, so its effectiveness is quite limited. This bureau, seeing this, has consulted with the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and reached an agreement that after the establishment of telephone lines in each district of Puxi is completed, they will be allowed to connect for mutual benefit. This matter is of great importance to the construction of each district, so a special letter is sent to invite you to come to this bureau at 2:00 PM on the 8th of this month to discuss the implementation."

City Propaganda Department Propaganda Meeting

The Fourteenth Meeting

The Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters Propaganda Department held its fourteenth city propaganda meeting at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. Those in attendance included Chen Dezheng and Xu Xingchu of the city propaganda department, and Huang Xianggu, Shen Ding, Shen Yu, Feng Xiancheng, Diao Qingen, Wu Xiqin, and over ten other district propaganda committee members. Department head Chen Dezheng presided over the meeting, with Zhou Hanmei taking notes. The meeting began with the usual formalities. First, the chairman reported, stating: "Today is the fourteenth city propaganda meeting. There are several matters to inform comrades of. First, the weather has been unusually hot recently, but the work of the city propaganda department is even more tense than the climate and cannot be relaxed. Currently, the department's efforts are focused on propaganda against the rebel, Wang Jingwei. Wang Jingwei followed our party leader, Dr. Sun Yat-sen, in the revolution for nearly twenty years. Thanks to Dr. Sun's constant instructions, he avoided falling into error. Comrades in our party praised him for his promising youth and hoped that he would benefit the party and the country and not disappoint Dr. Sun's earnest teaching. Who knew that after Dr. Sun's death, he would act as the leader, first colluding with his party and attempting to sell out our party, which Dr. Sun had painstakingly built, and then colluding with rebels Zhang Fakui and Tang Shengzhi, causing the tragic changes in Guangzhou and Hubei. While the pain of our people has not yet healed, Wang Jingwei not only did not close his door and reflect deeply but instead intensified his actions, colluding with warlord Feng, the Western Hills Conference faction, and the Communications Clique and Anfu Clique, and even colluding with warlords Qi Xieyuan and Sun Chuanfang, whom our party had already overthrown, creating a corrupt and evil group to overthrow the party and the country and reenact the warlord rule before 1926. Our party's Central Committee, upholding Dr. Sun's teachings and bearing the heavy responsibility of building, governing, and saving the country, should combine revolutionary force with the force of the people to directly attack the reactionary forces' lair and eliminate the heads of the traitors who harm the country. Over the past few months, the reactionary forces' strength has been almost completely destroyed, and their day of demise is not far off. However, the crimes of their betrayal of the party, harming the country, and harming the people should still be vigorously propagandized and exposed to the people of the entire country. Therefore, how to expand the propaganda against the rebels needs to be discussed in detail today. Second, the communist bandits in various places have become increasingly rampant. They previously captured Jingdezhen and recently captured Changsha. Although both have been recaptured, the pain suffered by the people is needless to say. Under the party's rule today, the more suffering the people have, the more responsibility our party has. In view of this, the guilt of our party comrades is deep, and how should our party comrades intensify their work to comfort Dr. Sun in the afterlife and save our people from misery? Subsequently, the district propaganda members successively reported on recent work. Then they began discussing (1) how to expand the propaganda against the rebels. It was resolved that (1) the City Propaganda Department should be requested to print a large number of posters and slogans and distribute them to party headquarters at all levels for posting, (2) the City Propaganda Department should be requested to publish special issues on propaganda against the rebels in Party Voice and Times, (3) the City Propaganda Department should be requested to order all districts to publish special issues on propaganda against the rebels in their regular publications, (4) the City Propaganda Department should be requested to hold an expanded memorial week next Monday to report on the latest situation in the fight against the rebels, and (5) the City Propaganda Department should be requested to order permanent propaganda teams in all districts to go out and spread propaganda. (2) The plan to improve the city's speech meetings was finalized. It was resolved to revise and approve it (the resolutions are very long, omitted here). The meeting was adjourned."

Notice to Probationary Party Members and Introducers

Deadline to Complete Procedures Within Today and Tomorrow

Overdue Submissions Will Invalidate Forms

The Organization Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters previously had some probationary party members' membership forms returned by the Central Committee for incomplete procedures and issued notices by letter and published announcements in the newspaper from the 28th of last month, ordering them to go to the department to complete the procedures from July 29th to the 7th of this month. This has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Now, there are only two days left until the deadline, and there are still a few probationary party members and introducers who have not completed the procedures. If they do not complete the procedures within today and tomorrow, their membership forms will be invalidated. Probationary party members or their introducers whose procedures are incomplete should pay attention to this. A list of their names is recorded below.

Sixth Anniversary of the National Anti-Drug Society

Declaration Issued Yesterday

The National Anti-Drug Society of China was founded on August 5, 1924, by over thirty public organizations from all walks of life in Shanghai. It has reached its sixth anniversary. Its years of struggle have been praised by people at home and abroad. Today, on the sixth anniversary of the society's founding, it has issued the following declaration: "Our country has suffered from the harm of opium for over a century. Those with knowledge all know that the harm of opium is sufficient to destroy the country and exterminate the race. It is more than just ruining oneself and destroying one's family. Over the years, repeated foreign defeats, the decline of national reputation, the poverty of people's livelihoods, and the encroachment of famine, and even the daily deterioration of public morals and the collapse of social customs, are all directly proportional to the harm of opium. The harm of opium deeply penetrates society and is closely related to the survival of the nation. Without combining the strength of the whole people to carry out an eradication movement, there is no way to save this endangered national destiny. The National Anti-Drug Society of China was born to shoulder this arduous mission, advocating a drug-resistance and nation-saving movement from the position of pure civilians, with the sole purpose of eliminating opium seedlings at home and stopping the import of drugs from abroad. Its working strategy is to use propaganda and education as the vanguard and promote smoking cessation as relief, hoping to create a strong public opinion with the public's consensus, internally to urge the government to implement prohibitive laws, and externally to use national diplomacy to connect with sympathetic groups in various countries to jointly limit the world's drug production. Scientific and medicinal uses are considered a long-term plan to address the root causes. Based on this scope, we have been working hard, with no political colors or factional effects, and without taking advantage of opportunities to seek anything. Since its establishment, we have been diligent and self-disciplined for six years, as if it were just one day. The people of the country are observing us. Colleagues are always vigilant, as if walking on thin ice, so as not to fail the public's trust and violate the purpose of eradicating opium. However, the devil is one foot taller than the Tao, which is true in ancient times and even more so today. Today, the scourge of drugs is rampant, increasing rather than decreasing, and the environmental situation is deteriorating day by day. The past achievements of this society, however small, all rely on the support of the people of the country. What we hope for from the people of the country in the future is even more cooperation. However, this society is not a judicial or administrative organ and has no power to enforce prohibition against the planting, transportation, trafficking, and smoking of opium, nor does it have the right to judge and punish. These powers are related to the central and local governments and cannot be overstepped by civil society groups. The Central Anti-Smoking Committee is an administrative organ. People from all sides do not understand the truth and often confuse it with this society. Some people are dissatisfied with the handling of previous opium cases and repeatedly question this society. It must be known that this society has no power and can do nothing. This society has always put forward opinions on the authorities' opium prohibition measures and urged them from the sidelines. Whether the propositions put forward are adopted and implemented depends entirely on the public opinion as a backing. Today, imperialists have not abandoned their opium policy, colonial governments still rely on tobacco taxes as their main source of income, and the remaining warlords and shameless bureaucrats still protect planting and trafficking for their own benefit. As for the local traffickers and opium merchants, they have great power, colluding with treacherous officials and bribing police detectives to do private business. All of these are in front of us. If we do not expand our organization and unite our strength, how can we curb this rampant flow and guide opium prohibition onto the right track? The success of alcohol prohibition in the United States relies entirely on the fifty years of unremitting struggle by people's groups. Our country's opium scourge is even worse than America's alcohol scourge. To achieve final success, it is necessary for the people of the entire country to contribute their spirit and strength to this great movement of humanity. It must be known that our enemies are united and have strong and well-organized organizations. If we do not cooperate, how can we overthrow the other side's power? As the military strategist said, 'Know yourself and know your enemy, and you will win every battle.' The anti-drug movement is also the same. This society has been fighting hard for many years and only knows that drug resistance is absolutely non-negotiable. We dare not change this will and have not changed our commitment. Success or failure is not what we care about. From now on, we must continue to uphold the entrustment of the people and work hard. We must ensure that this society exists for one day without changing. Now, on the occasion of the sixth anniversary of the founding of this society, and at the beginning of the implementation of the second five-year movement plan, we solemnly publish our vows in this declaration."

Japanese Trade Mission Arrives in Shanghai

The Japanese government, in order to develop trade with China, has appointed two overseas affairs officers to be stationed in Shanghai permanently. These officers have now been appointed and have arrived in Shanghai. One is Ota Rokuzo, who will be stationed in Shanghai, and the other is Takagi Kenzo, who will be stationed in Guangdong. Both are famous industrialists and businessmen from Nagoya. The Shanghai office will officially begin operating within days, with a trial period tentatively set for three years.

Preparations for the Chinese Institute of Engineers Annual Conference

The thirteenth annual conference of the Chinese Institute of Engineers has long been decided to be held in Shenyang from August 16th to 22nd. This has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The preparations for this annual conference are being carried out separately by the annual conference committee, the proposals committee, and the thesis committee. A brief description of the approximate situation is recorded below.

I. Regarding Proposals

The proposals for the conference are being prepared by Xu Peihuang, Xue Cixin, Zhu Youqian, Wei Ronghan, Zhang Zili, Zhang Kezhi, Tang Zhisu, Kong Xiange, and others. The most important proposals include: (1) retaining the same name after merging with the Chinese Engineers Association, (2) adding to the qualifications for membership, (3) allowing those who have made achievements in industry and passed a special examination by the association to become members, (4) reducing the membership fee for new members, and (5) adding rules for leaving the association, as well as other amendments to the constitution.

II. Regarding Theses

The theses for the conference are being prepared by Zhou Houkun, Hu Boyuan, Xu Mingcai, Yu Haomin, Zhu Xishang, Qian Changzuo, Chen Tirong, and others. The theses that have already been received are: (1) "Construction Method of Penetration Tar (Asphalt) Macadam Road and Surface-Treated Tar (Asphalt) Macadam Road" (Zhou Houkun), (2) "National Defense and Industry" (Feng Zhudi), (3) "Long-Distance Telephone Bridge Connection Method" (Chen Shaolin), (4) "Outline of the Yangtze River and Its Properties" (Song Ximian), (5) "Discussion on the Three-Phase AC Standard System" (Zhou Qi), (6) "Overview of the Water Supply of the Hankou Jiji Water and Electricity Company" (Qian Muning), (7) "The Past and Present of the Longhai Railway" (Li Yan), (8) "Research on Improving the Slope of the Beijing-Suiyuan Railway" (Liu Junfeng), (9) "Explanation of Liu's Inventory Calculation Manual" (Liu Zengmian), (10) "Electrical Network" (Yun Zhen), and (11) "Research on the Location of the Northeast Steel Plant" (Hu Shuhua). There are many more that are being sent in succession.

In addition to the usual conference agenda, this year's conference will also discuss the issue of merging with the Chinese Engineers Association, which is extremely important to the future of both associations and the engineering community. Moreover, there are many new engineering projects in the Northeast, which are sufficient to assist research. Therefore, the attendance of members is very enthusiastic.

City Chamber of Commerce Investigates the Total Capital of Various Shops

In Order to Collect Membership Fees Proportionately

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various industry associations yesterday regarding the collection of membership fees based on the total capital of various shops. The letter stated: "According to Article 30 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the expenses of the Chamber of Commerce are divided into the following two types: (1) Administrative expenses shall be borne by members in proportion to the number of representatives they send and their capital amount. When the former Preparatory Committee for the Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting of member representatives on June 21, it drafted a proposal to collect fees in proportion to the amount of capital, which was incorporated into Article 42 of the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce Constitution. This was discussed, revised, and approved by the member representatives at the meeting on that day and submitted to the Social Bureau for review. Since the use of the amount of capital as the standard for membership fees has already been stipulated in Article 30 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, it is necessary to investigate and clarify the total capital amount of the shops belonging to the group members and the capital amount of the company and shop members in order to provide a basis for collecting fees in proportion to the amount. Special letters are sent to inform you of this. It is hoped that your association will investigate and clarify the approximate total capital amount of the shops under your jurisdiction and reply to this association within two weeks for processing. If you fail to report within the deadline, this association will send personnel to investigate on its own in order to avoid delaying the process. We must first declare that the fees paid before the June 21 meeting of member representatives refer to the membership fees that should be added for each additional representative, which is different from the situation of investigating the amount of capital this time to determine the standard for collecting the basic membership fee that should be charged for sending one representative. If your association only sent one representative at that time, then after the amount of capital is clarified this time, the standard for collecting fees will be determined, and we will calculate whether you should receive a refund or pay an additional fee at that time. We are afraid that you have not examined this in detail and mistakenly think that this investigation is a duplicate collection of fees, so we will explain this in detail. Please also explain this to your association and handle it promptly."

Local News

Litigation Jurisdiction at the Border of the Chinese and Foreign Concessions

Accusation Against the Star Socks Factory

Rental Concession Number Affixed in Front

Location Within the Chinese Territory

Special District Court Declines Jurisdiction

The Star Socks Factory on North Szechuan Road was originally located in Chinese territory, but the road in front of it belonged to the concession. The factory's number, 482, was also assigned by the Municipal Council. This time, the factory was sued by the Stamp Office for not affixing stamps on invoices in accordance with stamp tax regulations. The Municipal Council notified the Special District Court to prosecute. Previously, its manager, He Zhongwen, was ordered to appear in court to await trial, but He did not appear. When the court opened again yesterday, He surrendered himself and declared that the socks factory was located in Chinese territory and not subject to the Special District Court's jurisdiction. Judge Luo Renji ruled that since the defendant was not under jurisdiction, the case should not be accepted. He then dismissed the charges. The detective lawyer had no objection to this decision. In recent years, there have been disputes between the police and Chinese authorities over jurisdiction in the area where the Chinese and foreign concessions meet on North Szechuan Road. Although these incidents have been short-lived and have not caused major disturbances, the future is long. If fundamental solutions are not found, the aftermath of foreign aggression is a cause for concern. Judge Luo's decision not only clarifies the jurisdiction of litigation but also deeply upholds the spirit of defending the country.

Over 300,000 Losses Due to Carelessness at Jardine Matheson Warehouse Yesterday Morning

Warehouse No. 8 Completely Destroyed

Cause of Fire Still Under Investigation

Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Warehouse No. 8 in Pudong's Lan Ni Du suddenly caught fire due to carelessness at around 2:00 AM yesterday, causing losses of approximately 300,000 in goods and the warehouse itself. A detailed investigation is recorded below:

Circumstances of the Fire

The company is located on the Pudong waterfront of Lan Ni Du, covering an area of over one hundred acres, with four large and small wharves, fourteen warehouses, and several offices for Chinese and Western personnel. Twelve petition police officers and one inspector from the Municipal Police Department's Third District were stationed inside the warehouse to provide protection. Unexpectedly, at 2:35 AM yesterday, Song Yulin, the night patrolman, smelled a burning odor near Warehouse No. 8 on the north side. He then saw thick black smoke coming out of the window seams of the warehouse. Knowing it was a fire, he immediately blew his whistle and reported to Inspector Jiang Jiming, who informed the Jardine Matheson Main Warehouse and used the telephone to alert various firefighting agencies on land and water.

Glimpse of Rescue Efforts

Soon, the internal burning intensified, and after about half an hour, it broke through the roof. The fire was raging, reaching high into the sky, and a red glow could be seen from afar. At this time, the Public Concession Municipal Council and the Customs Water Patrol Police sent firefighting boats to dock outside the warehouse and connected long hoses to pour water inside to extinguish the fire. By 5:00 AM, the fire gradually weakened, and after a while, the flames were extinguished. However, there were many items destroyed by the fire, which could not be completely extinguished easily. Yesterday morning, thick smoke was still visible, so the firefighting boats continued to work hard to draw water and spray it. Until the afternoon and evening, it had not stopped. Water flowed all over the fire scene inside and outside.

Embers of Jardine Matheson Warehouse No. 8 (Photo by This Newspaper's Photography Department)

Number of Losses

In this fire, in addition to the complete destruction of the burning Warehouse No. 8, an estimated 8,000 pieces of paper (each worth about eight taels of silver), 3,800 bags of soybeans (each worth about five taels of silver), 3,400 pieces of tea bricks (each worth about fifty taels of silver), 2,250 bags of wheat flour (each worth about two taels and five qian of silver), and three pieces of tobacco leaves were burned. The above goods were stored in the warehouse by various merchants, most of whom had fire insurance. It is reported that the total value of the losses, including the warehouse, is approximately 300,000 gold fire notes.

Cause Unknown

The company's warehouses open at 6:00 AM and lock at 5:00 PM every day. They employ warehouse specialists to manage the keys. No one lives in the warehouses, and smoking is prohibited when loading and unloading goods. The prevention is extremely strict, so the cause of the fire is still unknown. It is said that a handyman during the day may have accidentally dropped a cigarette butt into the pile of goods, which gradually burned and, after a long time, became a prairie fire, but this is not certain.

Police Patrol

When the fire started, Zhang, the district chief of the Third District of the Pudong Public Security Bureau, reported that strict precautions should be taken within the current martial law period. He immediately joined forces with Zhu, the captain of the Fourth Police Squad, to lead all police officers and distributed them around the warehouse to patrol back and forth to maintain order until dawn when they all returned to their teams.

Tragic Record of the Fire on Yuanfang Road

Cantonese Woman's Fire Causes Six or Seven Injuries

Injuries to Head, Neck, Legs, and Back Total Four

Mrs. Wang Wu Dies, Boy Buried in the Fire Pit

A Cantonese woman, the second landlord of No. 133 Donggui Lane, Yuanfang Road, Hongkou, was careless with fire at about 1:45 AM yesterday. Thick smoke billowed and flames lit up the sky. In an instant, the fire ladder burned down, preventing the residents upstairs from escaping. They jumped out of the windows one after another. Six or seven people fell and were injured. Wang Jinkui, 42, from Zhenjiang, a foreman at the Jardine Matheson Wharf, injured his back. Liu Xizi, 18, and Xi Guangren, 17, both from Gaoyou, injured their heads and legs. Fortunately, their injuries were mild. Mrs. Ou Sun, 34, from Yangzhou, broke her leg. Zhu Jin, 48, injured her neck and legs. All of the above were sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment. A young woman, Mrs. Wang Wu, 35, was burned all over her body and sent to Guangren Hospital, but she died at 5:00 PM yesterday because the rescue was ineffective. A boy surnamed, six months old, could not be rescued in time and was burned, his hands and feet destroyed, and he was buried in the fire pit. In this fire, a total of six houses were burned down. The fire was slightly extinguished until about 4:00 AM at dawn.

There are four rooms in the front row and three rooms in the back row, all bungalows, and land in Hongzhen, etc., which is not worth the price (Q). Yes, such as aunts and cousins, etc. After the interrogator got the testimony, he instructed the lawyers of both parties that the identity relationship should be studied first in this case. The debate will not be opened today. The hearing will be adjourned to another date. Then the court adjourned.

A Pitiful Prostitute's Life

Husband Died, Sold into a Brothel by Uncle

Soliciting Customers Every Night, Suffering Unspeakably

At about 8:40 AM yesterday, a young woman with fashionable clothes, about 20 years old, with a cropped haircut, was seen wandering and weeping on the road in Caojiadu Town, Jishiwei Road, West Shanghai. Her expression was very flustered, as if she had great worries. The passers-by stopped and watched. A member of the Fourth Team of the Songhu Security Regiment in the town saw her and immediately questioned her. Her words were vague and abnormal. Because her behavior was suspicious, she was taken back to the team headquarters. After questioning by the team leader, Li Meiqing, the woman claimed to be named Wang Liying, 20 years old, from Tangxi, Zhejiang, and lived at No. 8 Chengdeli, Touji Bridge, Public Concession. She married Chen Yuqing from the same village at the age of 17 through a matchmaker. After marriage, the couple's feelings were very close. Unexpectedly, good things are often ground down. After more than a year and a half, her husband suddenly died of illness. The woman was lost after losing her husband at a young age. She thought about making a living on her own and expressed her intention in conversation with others. Unexpectedly, it was heard by her husband's brother, Maoqing, who took the opportunity to lure the woman, falsely claiming that she could work in Shanghai and live without worry. He had acquaintances to introduce the woman. The woman believed him to be true and entered his trap. In mid-July last year, she came to Shanghai with her husband's brother, Maoqing. After staying in a hotel for a few days, he took the woman to Yuan's house at No. 8 Chengdeli and falsely claimed that she would learn peacefully here. He disappeared. When she saw that there were five or six women in the Yuan's house, she was surprised. The woman (i.e., the procuress) explained to the woman that you have been sold here by your uncle for 300 yuan. This place is a brothel and you must go out at night to receive customers. You must not be lazy, etc. The woman suddenly realized that she had been deceived. Therefore, regardless of sunny or rainy days, she must stand on the road at night to solicit customers and do this flesh-and-blood business. If there is any negligence, she will be whipped by the patrolmen on the outside and abused by the procuress inside all night without sleep. The procuress's abuse is really unspeakable. She wanted to jump out of the fire pit, but the surveillance was so strict that she could not succeed. Because of this, she was depressed and emaciated and her body was skinny and the sores on her lower body were severely inflamed, like suffering in hell. At about 2:00 AM yesterday morning, she happened to receive a guest surnamed Jin and stayed in Room 24 of the Zhongshan Hotel. Fortunately, the guest got up and left at 6:00 AM. The woman took this opportunity to escape. She was unfamiliar with the road and ran to this place. Her brain was really dizzy. She was grateful to be rescued, etc. After hearing the confession, Team Leader Li thought that the woman was deceived to Shanghai and sold as a prostitute and suffered abuse. Her life was really pitiful. He immediately sent a letter and sent someone to send the woman to the Zhabei Charity Group for support.

Wu A'mao Files a Lawsuit for Cohabitation

Reconciliation Achieved in Court

Husband and Wife Reunited

Wu A'mao, a native of this county, lives in Xin Jiekou, Lan Ni Du, Pudong. He hired Lawyer Qu to file a lawsuit for cohabitation with the local court. The defendant was originally a woman who became involved in the lawsuit due to a misunderstanding. After the court persuaded her, the suspicion was cleared. Wu Yu was allowed to live in her parents' home for ten days and return home. The defendant must not scold her, and the plaintiff must also abide by the way of women and not quarrel for no reason. Both parties promised without objection and considered the reconciliation established. The lady returned during the Dragon Boat Festival last year to spend time together until July, when she returned to Ning and did not return home. She was invited to return during the Qingming Festival this year, but she did not return. The husband and wife have the obligation to cohabit. The lady admitted that she would return home to spend time together, so how could she repent and never return after the incident? On July 9 this year, she entrusted her lawyer to send a letter agreeing to return home and live together peacefully within five days of receiving the letter. After more than ten days, there was still no news. She had no choice but to file a lawsuit requesting approval to check the original case and order the defendant to cohabit with the plaintiff, etc. The defendant, Wu Yu, also hired Zhu Fang as a lawyer to file a defense. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Judge Zhao Zhenhai opened the Fourth Court to hear the case. The plaintiff, Wu A'mao, testified about the previous situation. The defendant, Wu Yu, testified that because the plaintiff abused her, she temporarily lived in her mother's home, etc. The lawyers of both parties also stated their cases. Judge Zhao mediated and persuaded the defendant to return home and cohabit with the plaintiff, and the husband and wife reconciled. The defendant also expressed her willingness. Then the reconciliation was established and the husband and wife reunited. Both parties signed and withdrew from the court.

Good News for Waitress Gu Sanmei

Gu Sanmei, a waitress at the New New Company, is 19 years old, with bright eyes, white teeth, petite and exquisite. Therefore, a group of vagrants flocked to her. Her income is not bad and her clothes are fashionable, making her the best of the waitresses. Recently, she suddenly had a love affair with Zhou Kunhuai, a local. They lived together like a couple. Therefore, those who envied her became jealous and instigated Gu Sanmei's mother, Gu Xu, to sue her at the Special District Jiang Court for the crime of enticement. Gu Xu agreed without hesitation and was willing to reconcile, but proposed two conditions: (1) Gu Xu is willing to let her daughter Gu Sanmei live with Zhou Kunhuai forever. Sentencing Awaits in the Case of a Kitchen Helper Killing a Briton

The Murderer Admits He Did It Alone

Mr. Charles, a Briton who served in customs, was robbed in his bedroom on the third floor of No. 859 North Szechuan Road at 1:00 AM on the 19th of last month by Pan Zhi, a Cantonese kitchen helper, who killed him on the spot when he failed to seize the property. After the lawyers of both parties debated, Judge Ge Zhitan instructed the defendant to be returned to custody and sentenced on the 11th of this month.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Promotes the Conversion of Sanyi Lane to Tap Water

The well water in Sanyi Lane, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei is unclean and the water volume is insufficient. The tenants complain. The Municipal Public Works Bureau sent personnel to investigate and confirmed that it was difficult to improve the repair. In order to take care of the people's drinking plan, the bureau ordered the owner, Sanyi Company, to switch to tap water. The owner immediately contacted the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company and agreed, and ordered the Asian Heji Machinery Company, a water pipe company, to install water pipes, and paid the deposit and other fees to the water pipe company for transfer to the Water and Electricity Company. It is now known that water has been supplied for drinking on August 4. The bureau has also instructed the contractor on how to repair the remaining artesian well so that it can be used and not abandoned.

Shi Yueqin Commits Suicide in Desperation by Hanging

Shi Yueqin, a 40-year-old carpenter from Chongming, residing at Xinqiaotou, Xie Bridge, was addicted to opium and in dire straits. Shi previously worked for a fellow villager named Monk He, but during the Lunar New Year, when two apprentices of the monk went home, Shi pawned two of their cotton quilts without permission to get money for opium. After the two apprentices returned home and discovered this, Shi stopped working there. He was currently employed at the Yongda Metal and Wood Factory, located at No. 4, Lane 46, South Railway Station Back Road. Monk He, because Shi had not redeemed the quilts for a long time, went to his home for several days to demand them back. Shi, in desperation, went to the Yongda Factory yesterday morning and hanged himself with hemp rope from the beam in the kitchen. After he was discovered, the police were notified, who in turn notified the Second District Police Department. They instructed Gu Tiyun, the local head of the 25th Bao, 12th Tu, to report it to the local court. Prosecutor Xu and others arrived at the scene and, after investigation, instructed the family to collect the body for burial.

Lu Xubao Grieves Wife's Drowning

Zhang Xuerong Generously Offers Aid

The Shengda Rice Store, located at Nos. 32-33 Pishao Nai Road, outside Xiaobeimen, French Concession, is managed by Liang Hongying. The store regularly supplies rice to workers of the Tianmashan Mining Company, hiring boats from Shanghai to transport it. Recently, it was time again to deliver rice, and the store hired the boat of pier worker Lu Xubao to transport 30 shi of rice. They also assigned apprentice Zhang Xuerong (19 years old) to accompany the boat and oversee the delivery. On the first of this month, the boat arrived at the Huayang River estuary, not far from Tianmashan. The wife of the boat owner, Lu Xubao, attempted to walk from the stern along the edge to the bow when she accidentally fell into the river. The boat owner, Lu Xubao, upon seeing his wife fall into the river, immediately jumped in to save her. However, the current was very strong at the quadripartite river estuary, and there was also a strong wind. In an instant, the boat owner's wife disappeared, making rescue impossible. Lu Xubao was overcome with grief. The apprentice Zhang Xuerong, seeing the situation, showed courage and said to the boat owner Lu Xubao that he had 30 yuan in savings to offer him to help him retrieve his wife's body and handle the aftermath. Everyone on the boat praised the apprentice's noble act.

Jin Sanbao Seduces, Abducts, and Sells

Zhu Sanyuan Grossly Deceived

Zhu Mao, wife of Zhu Sanyuan, a villager from Zhujiaqiao, near Benniu in the western suburbs of Changzhou, is 29 years old. Though past her prime, she is still attractive, and the couple's relationship is quite harmonious. In the past two years, due to losses in silkworm farming (the western suburbs regard silkworm breeding as an important side business), they have accumulated a large debt, and the couple is constantly worried. A neighbor from the same village, Jin Sanbao, 26 years old, who works as a cook in a Shanghai mansion, returned to the village in May on some business. Seeing Zhu's family constantly harassed by creditors, and Zhu and his wife looking worried, he seized the opportunity and told Zhu that the factories in Shanghai were booming and lacking female workers. He said that if his wife went to Shanghai to work in a silk factory, she could earn a monthly salary of twenty or thirty yuan. If he was interested in his wife working in a factory, he would be able to secure an excellent job for her at the silk factory owned by his boss with a single word. Zhu was moved by his words and discussed it with Mao. Mao had also heard of Shanghai's prosperity and longed to visit, but had no opportunity. Seeing Jin’s willingness to introduce her to a job, she immediately agreed. They made preparations and left with Jin, while Zhu repeatedly entrusted her to Jin's care. On May 21, she traveled to Shanghai with Jin, carrying a bundle of clothes. Jin, however, was unemployed and had no place to live in Shanghai. He and Mao checked into a room at a small hotel on Rue Edouard, telling her that he needed to explain the situation to his boss before she could enter the factory. That night, he used all sorts of seductions, eventually raping her. The next day, Jin left and returned, telling Mao that his boss had gone to Putuo to burn incense and would return in a few days, so she would have to wait a little longer. They spent the room rent and used up all the clothes she had brought. Mao asked Jin daily whether his boss had returned, but Jin always gave excuses and delayed, saying that his boss would not return for a while, and he would have to recommend her to work as a helper in a wealthy family until his boss returned. Mao had no money for daily expenses and wanted to return to the village, but had no travel money, so she had to let him do as he pleased. Jin recommended her to work in a salted meat shop in Zhujiaqiao. In the beginning, the madam treated her well, but did not pay her any wages. Then she forced her to receive guests and engage in prostitution. Mao refused and asked the madam for wages, intending to take a car back to the village. The madam said that Jin Sanbao had pawned her to her, taking 50 yuan and stating that it was for a one-year term. If she wanted to leave, she would have to repay the 50 yuan. Mao was terrified and secretly sent a letter to her husband Zhu at a fortune-telling stall. Zhu came to Shanghai a few days ago and went to the salted meat shop to negotiate with the madam. He learned that he had been deceived by Jin and searched everywhere for Jin, but could not find him. He has now repeatedly pleaded with the madam, who has agreed to allow him to redeem his wife for 25 yuan. Therefore, Zhu has returned to his hometown to raise money to redeem his wife.

U.S. Department of Commerce Moves to Shanghai

Office Opens September 1st

The U.S. Embassy in China recently received instructions from the U.S. Department of Commerce approving the relocation of the Commercial Office attached to the U.S. Embassy in Peiping to Tianjin, where it will become a Commercial Branch. A Commercial Directorate-General will be established in Shanghai to oversee the three U.S. branches in China: Tianjin, Liaoning, and Hong Kong. This will be managed by the Commercial Counselor of the U.S. Embassy. With the relocation of the Directorate-General from Peiping to Shanghai, the center of gravity for business has shifted southward. The U.S. Commercial Counselor formerly stationed in Peiping will now be stationed permanently within the Shanghai Commercial Directorate. It is reported that the U.S. Commercial Directorate in Shanghai has already leased No. 3 Guangdong Road as its office and is scheduled to begin operations on that day. The reorganization has been communicated to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for transmission to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for their information.

After receiving the report, the association dispatched officers Wang Guan and Zhang Yueru to the scene to conduct an investigation. The details of the investigation are as follows: The victim is a five-year-old girl named Lu Xiaomei. She has been living as an adopted daughter of Lu Shiming from Haimen for over two years. Establishment of Navigation Channel Light Buoys in Dalian Bay

Notice from the Haiguan Haiwu Ke Xungongsi (Maritime Customs Surveying Department): This Surveying Department, after investigating the establishment of navigation channel light buoys in Dalian Bay, hereby lists the details as follows: According to the Dalian Port Bureau's June 25th notice, the South Manchuria Railway Company has established several gas light buoys to mark the navigation route to the Dalian Ganjingzi pier. The lights were lit around July 1st. The locations and markings are listed below: Dalian Area, Ganjingzi Navigation Channel, Light No. 1, located north of the Dalian port entrance, 57 degrees 17 minutes west, 3,160 meters away. The light uses a gas buoy, decorated in black, with a light 4 meters above the water surface. The light is visible from all sides, flashing white twice every four seconds, and visible for nine nautical miles in clear weather. Dalian Area, Ganjingzi Navigation Channel, Light No. 2, located east of the Dalian port entrance, 55 degrees 5 minutes west, 3,240 meters away. The light uses a gas buoy, decorated in red, with a light 4 meters above the water surface. The light is visible from all sides, flashing red twice every four seconds, and visible for nine nautical miles in clear weather. Dalian Area, Ganjingzi Navigation Channel, Light No. 3, located east of the Dalian port entrance, 1 degree 2 minutes east, 1,800 meters away. The light uses a gas buoy, decorated in black, with a light 3 meters above the water surface. The light is visible from all sides, flashing white once every three seconds, and visible for four nautical miles in clear weather. Dalian Area, Ganjingzi Navigation Channel, Light No. 4, located east of the Dalian port entrance, 1 degree 2 minutes east, 1,950 meters away. The light uses a gas buoy, decorated in red, with a light 3 meters above the water surface. The light is visible from all sides, flashing red once every three seconds, and visible for seven nautical miles in clear weather. Dalian Area, Ganjingzi Navigation Channel, Light No. 5, located east of the Dalian port entrance, 55 degrees 19 minutes east, 3,320 meters away. The light uses a gas buoy, decorated in black, with a light 3 meters above the water surface. The light is visible from all sides, flashing white once every four seconds (shining for two seconds and then extinguished for two seconds), and visible for seven nautical miles in clear weather. The actual longitude and latitude coordinates should be checked against the Japanese government's Hydrographic Department's nautical charts Nos. 380 and 396. All vessels should pay attention to these details to avoid accidents. Do not forget! This notice is issued on July 5th, 1920.

They stopped a woman named Chen Gao under the pretext of searching for contraband and forcibly stole 50 yuan in banknotes from her pocket before fleeing. Mrs. Chen shouted for help, and patrolmen heard her cries, apprehended Ni and He, and took them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought before the French court for prosecution. The plaintiff testified about the robbery. Ni and He confessed to the robbery without hesitation. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Ni to two months in a Western prison and He to one month as a warning.

Another Gambling Den Found in the French Concession Yesterday

Yu Gengsheng and Yang A'kang have recently been running an illegal gambling den in the French Concession, enticing people to gamble through secret codes. This was discovered by detectives from the French police, who raided the premises the other day and seized gambling records, silver dollars, and other items. They were taken to the police station and brought before the French court yesterday. The police chief reported the situation. The two defendants confessed to running the illegal gambling den. The judge fined them 50 yuan each, to be confiscated.

Thieves Sentenced to One Month

Theives Wang Yongfa and Wu Aqing, on the other day, went to No. 210 Rue Massenet in the French Concession, pretending to be patients seeking treatment at the Western doctor Kong Deping's house. They sneaked into the house and stole three sets of Western-style clothes worth over 100 yuan before fleeing. They pawned the stolen goods. French police detectives discovered this, apprehended Wang and Wu, recovered the stolen items, and took them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought before the French court for prosecution. The plaintiff testified. The defendants confessed to the theft without hesitation. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Wang and Wu to one month each in a Western prison as a warning.

Shanghai County Second District to Issue Medical Assistance Certificates

Peng Liren, the head of the Second District of Shanghai County, recognizing that diseases are prevalent between summer and autumn and that poor people cannot afford medical treatment, urgently needs to find ways to provide relief. The previous system of setting up clinics required fixed dates, preventing timely diagnosis and treatment. Both doctors and patients had to travel long distances to the clinic, which was inconvenient. Therefore, he intends to change to a certificate system. The district office will print medical assistance certificates and issue them to various township offices. Poor patients can go to the nearest township office to obtain a certificate and then consult a doctor at their home. This method is more convenient. He invited all the district doctors to a meeting yesterday to discuss the proposal, and it was unanimously approved. The medical assistance certificates have been sent to Shanghai for printing and will be distributed soon.

Director Cao Solves a Case and Captures Criminals

On the afternoon of July 30th, at 5:00 PM, the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau received a letter from the surveying team of the Land Bureau, currently stationed at No. 1 Lianhua Nunnery, Huangjiazhai, stating that the team was robbed and looted unsuccessfully at 2:00 AM on July 27th and requesting an investigation. Cao Chengbing, the director of the precinct, immediately led Patrol Leader Liu Qingyun and patrolman Zhang Congsi to investigate. It was verified that the team had been robbed and looted unsuccessfully. After the verification, they returned to the precinct and carefully investigated the route taken by the criminals. Near Chenjiatou, they smelled the odor of opium and traced it to the Wu Gengsheng Teahouse at No. 7. They apprehended one set of smoking paraphernalia and two liang of opium on the spot and confiscated a Browning pistol containing seven rounds of live ammunition. Witnesses were also apprehended and taken to the headquarters for investigation.

Jiufu Company Introduces New Tonic "Bulido"

Jiufu Company on Rue Amiral Bayle has successfully developed a new type of modified tonic called Bulido. There are two types: Pure and Fortified with Strychnine. Those who are generally weak and want to become stronger can take Pure Bulido. Those with consumption, coughs, and other debilitating conditions can take Fortified with Strychnine Bulido. It has a delicious taste and great efficacy. It is sold in all major pharmacies on the market.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor,

Regarding the news item I saw in your esteemed newspaper about the 7th Executive Committee meeting of the National Medical Association, specifically point five of the matters discussed by the association, concerning the Central University Medical College sending Mr. Reiss, a Chinese representative, to attend the International Medical Congress, which concerns the dignity of our country's scholars, and the association urgently needing to express its views. The resolution was to send a letter warning the Central University Medical College, instructing it to consider the national interest, promote academics, and re-appoint a Chinese scholar as a representative. If it is difficult to choose, it is better to be absent. If a foreigner is the representative, the association should send a telegram to the International Medical Congress to deny it, and so on. Upon investigation, Dr. Reiss Luo has always been an associate professor of dermatology at our college. This time, he is going back to his country on leave to participate in the International Dermatology Congress in The Hague in a personal capacity. Our college has not entrusted him with the appointment of a representative, and the association does not have an explicit invitation to send a representative. Our college also has no need to appoint a representative. The various sections discussed by the Executive Committee of the National Medical Association are completely inconsistent with the facts. For the sake of the reputation of our college, in addition to sending a letter to the Medical Association to correct the facts, this is a solemn statement, requesting your esteemed newspaper to publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" section. Thank you very much. Please give my regards to the editor.

National Central University Medical College, August 5th

To the Editor,

Upon reviewing today's (August 5th) local news column in your esteemed newspaper, regarding "Chongsha Shipping's Mediation of Tidal Disputes Breaks Down," the fact that the mediation of this case failed to reach a settlement is indeed true, but other records contain many errors. I am writing to you urgently to request a correction to clarify the situation and show the friendship of the public. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Shipping Association Editorial Department of the Shen Bao, 1985.

To the Editor,

I recently read a news item in yesterday's newspaper about the German Constitution Day anniversary, which stated that the German Consulate General in this city will hold a commemorative ceremony at the consulate from 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM on the 11th of this month, and will host foreign guests from various countries. After investigation, the reception for guests on that day will be from 11:30 AM to 12:30 PM, not 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM. This is specially reported and it is hoped that it will be corrected. Respectfully addressed to the Editorial Department of the Shen Bao, German Consulate General in Shanghai, August 5th.
